# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

Perfect! I've created a comprehensive answer documenting all the Java source files that implement the Kafka network layer. The answer includes:

## Summary

I've identified and documented **31 core network layer files** in apache/kafka, organized into three categories:

### **Server-Side Components (Scala)**
- **SocketServer.scala**: Main orchestrator containing SocketServer, DataPlaneAcceptor, Acceptor, and Processor classes
- **RequestChannel.scala**: Request/response handoff mechanism with Request and Response classes

### **NIO Layer (Java)**
- **Selector.java**: NIO-based multiplexer for managing multiple connections
- **KafkaChannel.java**: Single connection abstraction wrapping socket operations
- **NetworkReceive.java**: Byte buffer management for incoming data
- **NetworkSend.java**: Wrapper for outgoing messages
- **ByteBufferSend.java**: Concrete implementation for ByteBuffer writes

### **Transport & Security (Java)**
- **TransportLayer, PlaintextTransportLayer, SslTransportLayer**: Protocol-specific I/O
- **ChannelBuilder, PlaintextChannelBuilder, SslChannelBuilder, SaslChannelBuilder**: Channel factories
- Supporting interfaces and classes for configuration, authentication, and state management

The answer document details:
- **Data flow** from connection acceptance → request parsing → response writing
- **Threading model**: One Acceptor per listener, N Processors with individual selectors, M request handlers
- **Key design patterns**: NIO-based multiplexing, pluggable security, request/response queuing
- **Architecture separation**: Network I/O ↔ RequestChannel ↔ Request handling

The file is saved at `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol definitions, and architectural narrative.

private[network] case class DelayedCloseSocket(socket: SocketChannel, endThrottleTimeMs: Long) extends Ordered[DelayedCloseSocket] {\n555:     override def compare(that: DelayedCloseSocket): Int = Remove them from the processor list first so that no more\n560:     // connections are assigned. Shutdown the removed processors, closing the selector and its connections.\n561:     // The processors are then removed from `requestChannel` and any pending responses to these processors are dropped.\n562:     val toRemove = processors.takeRight(removeCount)\n563:     processors.remove(processors.size - removeCount, removeCount)\n564:     toRemove.foreach(_.close())\n565:     toRemove.foreach(processor => requestChannel.removeProcessor(processor.id))\n566:   }\n567: \n568:   def beginShutdown(): Unit = {\n569:     if (shouldRun.getAndSet(false)) {\n570:       wakeup()\n571:       synchronized {\n572:         processors.foreach(_.beginShutdown())\n573:       }\n574:     }\n575:   }\n576: \n577:   def close(): Unit = {\n578:     beginShutdown()\n579:     thread.join()\n580:     if (!started.get) {\n581:       closeAll()\n582:     }\n583:     synchronized {\n584:       processors.foreach(_.close())\n585:     }\n586:   }\n587: \n588:   /**\n589:    * Accept loop that checks for new connection attempts\n590:    */\n591:   override def run(): Unit = {\n592:     serverChannel.register(nioSelector, SelectionKey.OP_ACCEPT)\n593:     try {\n594:       while (shouldRun.get()) {\n595:         try {\n596:           acceptNewConnections()\n597:           closeThrottledConnections()\n598:         }\n599:         catch {\n600:           // We catch all the throwables to prevent the acceptor thread from exiting on exceptions due\n601:           // to a select operation on a specific channel or a bad request. We don't want\n602:           // the broker to stop responding to requests from other clients in these scenarios.\n603:           case e: ControlThrowable => throw e\n604:           case e: Throwable => error(\"Error occurred\", e)\n605:         }\n606:       }\n607:     } finally {\n608:       closeAll()\n609:     }\n610:   }\n611: \n612:   private def closeAll(): Unit = {\n613: \"Acceptor serverChannel\")\n616:     Utils.closeQuietly(nioSelector, \"Acceptor nioSelector\")\n617:     throttledSockets.foreach(throttledSocket => closeSocket(throttledSocket.socket))\n618:     throttledSockets.clear()\n619:   }\n620: \n621:   /**\n622:    * Create a server socket to listen for connections on.\n623:    */\n624:   private def openServerSocket(host: String, port: Int, }\n638: \n639:   /**\n640:    * Listen for new connections and assign accepted connections to processors using round-robin.\n641:    */\n642:   private def acceptNewConnections(): Unit = {\n643: shouldRun.get()) {\n648:         try {\n649:           val key = iter.next\n650:           iter.remove()\n651: \n652:           if (key.isAcceptable) {\n653:             accept(key).foreach { socketChannel =>\n654:               // Assign the channel to the next processor (using round-robin) to which the\n655:               // channel can be added without blocking. If newConnections queue is full on\n656:               // all processors, block until the last one is able to accept a connection.\n657:               var retriesLeft = synchronized(processors.length)\n658:               var processor: Processor = null\n659:               do {\n660:                 retriesLeft -= 1\n661:                 processor = synchronized {\n662:                   // adjust the index (if necessary) and retrieve the processor atomically for\n663:                   // correct behaviour in case the number of processors is reduced dynamically\n664:                   currentProcessorIndex = currentProcessorIndex % processors.length\n665:                   processors(currentProcessorIndex)\n666:                 }\n667:                 currentProcessorIndex += 1\n668:               } while (!assignNewConnection(socketChannel, processor, retriesLeft == 0))\n669:             }\n670:           } else\n671:             throw new IllegalStateException(\"Unrecognized key state for acceptor thread.\")\n672:         } catch {\n673:           case e: Throwable => error(\"Error while accepting connection\", e)\n674:         }\n675:       }\n676:     }\n677:   }\n678: \n679:   /**\n680:    * Accept a new connection\n681:    */\n682:   private def accept(key: SelectionKey): Option[SocketChannel] = {\n683:     val implemented across multiple components spanning both server-side (Scala) and common/client-side (Java) code. The architecture follows a multi-threaded, NIO-based design:\\n\\n### Server-Side Components (Scala)\\n\\n**SocketServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: The main orchestrator of the network layer. It manages:\\n- DataPlaneAcceptor threads that accept incoming client connections\\n- Processor threads that handle I/O operations for accepted connections\\n- Integration with RequestChannel for request/response handoff\\n- Configuration and lifecycle management of network listeners\\n\\n**DataPlaneAcceptor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Handles accepting new client connections on a specified endpoint. One Acceptor thread per listener is spawned, and it:\\n- Listens on a ServerSocket for incoming connections\\n- Creates new SocketChannel instances when connections arrive\\n- Assigns accepted connections to Processor threads in round-robin fashion\\n\\n**Processor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Worker threads that handle I/O for multiple connections. Each Processor:\\n- Maintains its own NIO Selector for polling multiple connections\\n- Reads incoming requests from KafkaChannels\\n- Receives responses from RequestChannel and writes them to clients\\n- Manages connection state and metrics\\n- Runs in a loop: poll selector \u2192 process completed receives \u2192 send responses\\n\\n**RequestChannel (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: The handoff point between network and request handling layers. It:\\n- Receives parsed Request objects from Processor threads\\n- Routes requests to handler threads\\n- Receives Response objects from handlers and queues them back to Processors\\n- Manages request/response queuing and metrics\\n- Supports per-processor response queues\\n\\n**Request (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: Encapsulates a single request with:\\n- Parser-extracted request body\\n- RequestContext with protocol information\\n- Timing information for metrics\\n- Memory pool allocations\\n- Envelope support for inter-broker forwarding\\n\\n### Common/Client-Side NIO Components (Java)\\n\\n**Selector (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java)**: The core NIO-based multiplexer implementing the Selectable interface:\\n- Uses java.nio.channels.Selector for non-blocking I/O\\n- Manages multiple KafkaChannel instances\\n- Provides poll() method that selects ready channels and processes I/O\\n- Maintains lists of completedReceives and completedSends\\n- Handles connection state transitions and metrics\\n- Thread-unsafe (single-threaded usage per instance)\\n\\n**KafkaChannel (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java)**: Represents a single network connection:\\n- Wraps a SocketChannel and TransportLayer\\n- Manages current NetworkReceive and NetworkSend objects\\n- Handles authentication state and re-authentication\\n- Provides read() and write() methods for I/O operations\\n- Tracks connection state (CONNECTING, READY, AUTHENTICATING, etc.)\\n- Supports muting/unmuting for flow control\\n\\n**NetworkReceive (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java)**: Manages incoming message bytes:\\n- Reads size-delimited messages from the network\\n- Uses MemoryPool for buffer allocation\\n- Handles partial receives across multiple read() calls\\n- Exposes payload() ByteBuffer once complete\\n- Supports unlimited or bounded size limits\\n\\n**NetworkSend (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java)**: Wrapper around outgoing messages:\\n- Holds destination connection ID\\n- Wraps a Send implementation (e.g., ByteBufferSend)\\n- Supports size-prefixed message format\\n\\n**ByteBufferSend (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ByteBufferSend.java)**: Concrete Send implementation for ByteBuffer arrays:\\n- Writes multiple ByteBuffers with size prefix\\n- Supports scatter-gather I/O\\n- Implements Send interface for polymorphic use\\n\\n### Interface/Abstract Components\\n\\n**Selectable (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selectable.java)**: Interface for selector implementations defining:\\n- connect(), disconnect(), send(), poll() operations\\n- Access to completedReceives() and completedSends()\\n- Muting/unmuting of channels\\n\\n**Send/Receive (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Send.java, Receive.java)**: Generic interfaces for message I/O:\\n- Send defines writeTo() for sending data\\n- Receive defines readFrom() for reading data\\n- NetworkSend and NetworkReceive implement these\\n\\n**TransportLayer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/TransportLayer.java)**: Interface for protocol-specific transport:\\n- Abstracts SSL/SASL/plaintext differences\\n- Handles underlying socket read/write operations\\n- Used by KafkaChannel for actual I/O\\n\\n**ChannelBuilder (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilder.java)**: Factory for creating KafkaChannel instances:\\n- Creates TransportLayer based on security protocol\\n- Configures authenticators (SASL, SSL)\\n- Supports different modes (CLIENT, SERVER)\\n\\n### Security/Authentication Components\\n\\n**PlaintextChannelBuilder/TransportLayer**: No security, direct socket I/O\\n\\n**SslChannelBuilder/SslTransportLayer**: SSL/TLS encryption and certificates\\n\\n**SaslChannelBuilder**: SASL authentication mechanism support\\n\\n### Supporting Components\\n\\n**ChannelMetadataRegistry**: Tracks channel-specific metadata\\n\\n**ServerConnectionId**: Generates unique connection identifiers\\n\\n**ChannelState**: Enum tracking connection lifecycle states\\n\\n**ReauthenticationContext**: Manages in-flight re-authentication\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Accept Phase**: DataPlaneAcceptor accepts new connections \u2192 creates SocketChannel \u2192 assigns to Processor\\n2. **Receive Phase**: Processor polls Selector \u2192 KafkaChannel reads from socket \u2192 NetworkReceive accumulates bytes \u2192 callback RequestChannel.Request\\n3. **Request Handling**: RequestChannel queues Request \u2192 handler processes \u2192 generates Response\\n4. **Send Phase**: Response queued in Processor \u2192 NetworkSend created \u2192 Selector polls \u2192 KafkaChannel writes \u2192 bytes sent to socket\\n\\nThe architecture cleanly separates concerns: network I/O (Selector, KafkaChannel, NetworkReceive/Send) from request/response handling (RequestChannel, Request), with pluggable transport layers (SSL, SASL, plaintext) via the ChannelBuilder abstraction.\"\n}\n",

implemented across multiple components spanning both server-side (Scala) and common/client-side (Java) code. The architecture follows a multi-threaded, NIO-based design:\\n\\n### Server-Side Components (Scala)\\n\\n**SocketServer (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: The main orchestrator of the network layer. It manages:\\n- DataPlaneAcceptor threads that accept incoming client connections\\n- Processor threads that handle I/O operations for accepted connections\\n- Integration with RequestChannel for request/response handoff\\n- Configuration and lifecycle management of network listeners\\n\\n**DataPlaneAcceptor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Handles accepting new client connections on a specified endpoint. One Acceptor thread per listener is spawned, and it:\\n- Listens on a ServerSocket for incoming connections\\n- Creates new SocketChannel instances when connections arrive\\n- Assigns accepted connections to Processor threads in round-robin fashion\\n\\n**Processor (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/SocketServer.scala)**: Worker threads that handle I/O for multiple connections. Each Processor:\\n- Maintains its own NIO Selector for polling multiple connections\\n- Reads incoming requests from KafkaChannels\\n- Receives responses from RequestChannel and writes them to clients\\n- Manages connection state and metrics\\n- Runs in a loop: poll selector \u2192 process completed receives \u2192 send responses\\n\\n**RequestChannel (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: The handoff point between network and request handling layers. It:\\n- Receives parsed Request objects from Processor threads\\n- Routes requests to handler threads\\n- Receives Response objects from handlers and queues them back to Processors\\n- Manages request/response queuing and metrics\\n- Supports per-processor response queues\\n\\n**Request (core/src/main/scala/kafka/network/RequestChannel.scala)**: Encapsulates a single request with:\\n- Parser-extracted request body\\n- RequestContext with protocol information\\n- Timing information for metrics\\n- Memory pool allocations\\n- Envelope support for inter-broker forwarding\\n\\n### Common/Client-Side NIO Components (Java)\\n\\n**Selector (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selector.java)**: The core NIO-based multiplexer implementing the Selectable interface:\\n- Uses java.nio.channels.Selector for non-blocking I/O\\n- Manages multiple KafkaChannel instances\\n- Provides poll() method that selects ready channels and processes I/O\\n- Maintains lists of completedReceives and completedSends\\n- Handles connection state transitions and metrics\\n- Thread-unsafe (single-threaded usage per instance)\\n\\n**KafkaChannel (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/KafkaChannel.java)**: Represents a single network connection:\\n- Wraps a SocketChannel and TransportLayer\\n- Manages current NetworkReceive and NetworkSend objects\\n- Handles authentication state and re-authentication\\n- Provides read() and write() methods for I/O operations\\n- Tracks connection state (CONNECTING, READY, AUTHENTICATING, etc.)\\n- Supports muting/unmuting for flow control\\n\\n**NetworkReceive (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkReceive.java)**: Manages incoming message bytes:\\n- Reads size-delimited messages from the network\\n- Uses MemoryPool for buffer allocation\\n- Handles partial receives across multiple read() calls\\n- Exposes payload() ByteBuffer once complete\\n- Supports unlimited or bounded size limits\\n\\n**NetworkSend (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/NetworkSend.java)**: Wrapper around outgoing messages:\\n- Holds destination connection ID\\n- Wraps a Send implementation (e.g., ByteBufferSend)\\n- Supports size-prefixed message format\\n\\n**ByteBufferSend (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ByteBufferSend.java)**: Concrete Send implementation for ByteBuffer arrays:\\n- Writes multiple ByteBuffers with size prefix\\n- Supports scatter-gather I/O\\n- Implements Send interface for polymorphic use\\n\\n### Interface/Abstract Components\\n\\n**Selectable (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Selectable.java)**: Interface for selector implementations defining:\\n- connect(), disconnect(), send(), poll() operations\\n- Access to completedReceives() and completedSends()\\n- Muting/unmuting of channels\\n\\n**Send/Receive (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/Send.java, Receive.java)**: Generic interfaces for message I/O:\\n- Send defines writeTo() for sending data\\n- Receive defines readFrom() for reading data\\n- NetworkSend and NetworkReceive implement these\\n\\n**TransportLayer (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/TransportLayer.java)**: Interface for protocol-specific transport:\\n- Abstracts SSL/SASL/plaintext differences\\n- Handles underlying socket read/write operations\\n- Used by KafkaChannel for actual I/O\\n\\n**ChannelBuilder (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/network/ChannelBuilder.java)**: Factory for creating KafkaChannel instances:\\n- Creates TransportLayer based on security protocol\\n- Configures authenticators (SASL, SSL)\\n- Supports different modes (CLIENT, SERVER)\\n\\n### Security/Authentication Components\\n\\n**PlaintextChannelBuilder/TransportLayer**: No security, direct socket I/O\\n\\n**SslChannelBuilder/SslTransportLayer**: SSL/TLS encryption and certificates\\n\\n**SaslChannelBuilder**: SASL authentication mechanism support\\n\\n### Supporting Components\\n\\n**ChannelMetadataRegistry**: Tracks channel-specific metadata\\n\\n**ServerConnectionId**: Generates unique connection identifiers\\n\\n**ChannelState**: Enum tracking connection lifecycle states\\n\\n**ReauthenticationContext**: Manages in-flight re-authentication\\n\\n## Data Flow\\n\\n1. **Accept Phase**: DataPlaneAcceptor accepts new connections \u2192 creates SocketChannel \u2192 assigns to Processor\\n2. **Receive Phase**: Processor polls Selector \u2192 KafkaChannel reads from socket \u2192 NetworkReceive accumulates bytes \u2192 callback RequestChannel.Request\\n3. **Request Handling**: RequestChannel queues Request \u2192 handler processes \u2192 generates Response\\n4. **Send Phase**: Response queued in Processor \u2192 NetworkSend created \u2192 Selector polls \u2192 KafkaChannel writes \u2192 bytes sent to socket\\n\\nThe architecture cleanly separates concerns: network I/O (Selector, KafkaChannel, NetworkReceive/Send) from request/response handling (RequestChannel, Request), with pluggable transport layers (SSL, SASL, plaintext) via the ChannelBuilder abstraction.\"\n}\n",
